and which does not.\n\tvar leftRuleLine, leftRuleStart, leftRuleEnd string\n\tvar leftRuleWidth int // in visual character cells\n\n\tswitch diag.Severity {\n\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityError:\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][red]Error: [reset]\"))\n\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[red]│[reset] \")\n\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[red]╷[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[red]╵[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityWarning:\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][yellow]Warning: [reset]\"))\n\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[yellow]│[reset] \")\n\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[yellow]╷[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[yellow]╵[reset]\")\n\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// Clear out any coloring that might be applied by Terraform's UI helper,\n\t\t// so our result is not context-sensitive.\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"\\n[reset]\"))\n\t}\n\n\t// We don't wrap the summary, since we expect it to be terse, and since\n\t// this is where we put the text of a native Go error it may not always\n\t// be pure text that lends itself well to word-wrapping.\n\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, color.Color(\"[bold]%s[reset]\\n\\n\"), uint(paraWidth))\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", line)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", diag.Detail)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Before we return, we'll finally add the left rule prefixes to each\n\t// line so that the overall message is visually delimited from what's\n\t// around it. ruleBuf.String()\n}\n\n// DiagnosticPlain is an alternative to Diagnostic which minimises the use of\n// virtual terminal formatting sequences.\n//\n// It is intended for use in automation and other contexts in which diagnostic\n// messages are parsed from the Terraform output.\nfunc DiagnosticPlain(diag tfdiags.Diagnostic, sources map[string][]byte, width int) string {\n\treturn can be different if the\n   223→\t// previous resource instance was subject to a \"moved\" block that we\n   224→\t// handled in the process of creating this plan.\n   225→\t//\n   226→\t// For the In that case,\n   238→\t// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that\n   239→\t// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.\n   240→\tDeposedKey states.DeposedKey\n   241→\n   242→\t// Provider is the address of the provider configuration that was used\n   243→\t// to plan this change, and thus the configuration that must also be\n   244→\t// used to apply it.\n   245→\tProviderAddr addrs.AbsProviderConfig\n   246→\n   247→\t// Change is an embedded description of the change.\n   248→\tChange\n   249→\n   250→\t// ActionReason is an optional extra indication of why we chose the\n   251→\t// action recorded in Change.Action for this particular resource instance.\n   252→\t//\n   253→\t// This is an approximate mechanism only for the purpose of explaining the\n   254→\t// plan to end-users in the UI and is not to be used for any\n   255→\t// decision-making during the apply step; if apply behavior needs to vary\n   256→\t// depending on the \"action reason\" then the information for that decision\n   257→\t// must be recorded more precisely elsewhere for that purpose.\n   258→\t//\n   259→\t// Sometimes there might be more than one reason for choosing a particular\n   260→\t// action. In that case, it's up to the codepath making that decision to\n   261→\t// decide which value would provide the most relevant explanation to the\n   262→\t// end-user and return that. Pass the type constraint\n   603→// that the values are expected to conform to; to properly decode the values\n   604→// later an identical type constraint must be provided at that time.\n   605→//\n   606→// Where a Change is embedded in some other struct, it's generally better\n   607→// to call the corresponding Encode method of that struct rather than working\n   608→// directly with its embedded Change.\n   609→func (c *Change) Encode(ty cty.Type) (*ChangeSrc, error) {\n   610→\t// We can't serialize value marks directly so we'll need to extract the\n   611→\t// sensitive marks and store them in a separate field.\n   612→\t//\n   613→\t// We don't accept any other marks here. Therefore only root\n\t// module outputs will survive a round-trip through a plan file.\n\tOutputs []*OutputChange\n}\n\n// NewChanges returns a valid Changes object that describes no changes.\nfunc NewChanges() *Changes {\n\treturn &Changes{}\n}\n\n// Encode encodes all the stored resource and output changes into a new *ChangeSrc value\nfunc (c *Changes) Encode(schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) (*ChangesSrc, error) {\n\t// a plan is always built even when there are errors, so make sure to return\n\t// a valid changesSrc.\n\tchangesSrc := NewChangesSrc()\n\n\tfor _, rc := range c.Resources {\n\t\tp, ok := schemas.Providers[rc.ProviderAddr.Provider]\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\treturn changesSrc, fmt.Errorf(\"Changes.Encode: missing provider %s for %s\", rc.ProviderAddr, rc.Addr)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar schema providers.Schema\n\t\tswitch rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode {\n\t\tcase addrs.ManagedResourceMode:\n\t\t\tschema = p.ResourceTypes[rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type]\n\t\tcase addrs.DataResourceMode:\n\t\t\tschema = p.DataSources[rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type]\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unexpected resource mode %s\", rc.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode))\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif schema.Block == nil {\n\t\t\treturn changesSrc, fmt.Errorf(\"Changes.Encode: missing schema for %s\", rc.Addr)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\trcs, err := rc.Encode(schema.Block.ImpliedType())\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn changesSrc, fmt.Errorf(\"Changes.Encode: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tchangesSrc.Resources = append(changesSrc.Resources, rcs)\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, ocs := range c.Outputs {\n\t\toc, err := ocs.Encode()\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn changesSrc, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tchangesSrc.Outputs = append(changesSrc.Outputs, oc)\n\t}\n\n\treturn changesSrc, nil\n}\n\n// ResourceInstance returns the planned change for the current object of the\n// resource instance of the given address, if any. 145→\n   146→// AppendResourceInstanceChange records the given resource instance change in\n   147→// the set of planned resource changes.\n   148→func (c *ChangesSrc) resource type's schema type to method Decode to\n   159→// obtain a ResourceInstanceChange.\n   160→type ResourceInstanceChangeSrc struct {\n   161→\t// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change\n   162→\t// will apply to.\n   163→\t//\n   164→\t// THIS IS NOT A SUFFICIENT UNIQUE IDENTIFIER! It doesn't consider the\n   165→\t// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be\n   166→\t// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you\n   167→\t// need a unique address for a particular change.\n   168→\tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n   169→\n   170→\t// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the\n   171→\t// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the\n   172→\t// current object.\n   173→\t//\n   174→\t// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will\n   175→\t// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. 74→\t// Sort all lists for consistent output\n    75→\tsort.Strings(changes.creates)\n    76→\tsort.Strings(changes.updates)\n    77→\tsort.Strings(changes.deletes)\n struct{}\n\n// Format produces a compact summary of the plan's changes grouped by action type.\n//\n// The output includes one line per resource change in the format:\n//   [action] []string{},\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t// Skip deposed resources\n\t\tif rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\taddr := append(changes.forgets, addr)\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tchanges.other = append(changes.other, addr)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Sort all lists for consistent append(changes.forgets, addr)\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tchanges.other = append(changes.other, addr)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Sort all lists for consistent
